So any matching candidate must (i) have exactly a \(\sqrt{A}\) term with coefficient \(-0.2596...\), (ii) have exactly a \(\cos(\log(A+1))\) term with coefficient \(0.9123...\), (iii) have no extra dependence on \(t\), and (iv) not introduce other functional forms (extra sin/cos at different frequencies, exponentials, rationals in \(A\), logs outside cosine, etc.). Also note many candidates use `Abs(A)`; that cannot equal \(\sqrt{A}\) behavior on all real \(A\), and even restricting to \(A\ge 0\), \(\cos(\log(|A|+1))=\cos(\log(A+1))\) is fine, but we still need the \(-\sqrt{A}\) term.

Now check each candidate for whether it can be parameter-set to exactly the GT for all \(A,t\).

1. \(c0 + c1\cos(c2\log(c3|A|+1)) + c4\sin(\dots)\). Can match the cosine part by setting \(c2=1,c3=1,c1=0.9123\) and kill the sine with \(c4=0\), but there is no \(\sqrt{A}\) term. Cannot match.

Remaining issue: candidate uses \(A^{c0}\) (not \(|A|^{c0}\)), so for negative \(A\) it is not real; GT also is not real for negative \(A\) because of \(\sqrt{A}\) and \(\log(A+1)\). Also need no extra constant: set \(c2=0\). This candidate *can* be made identical to GT on the natural real domain \(A\ge 0\). Under the problem’s “for all values of the feature variables” wording, if interpreted as “for all real \(A\) where both sides are defined as real”, this matches. Keep checking others, but this is already a viable match.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT:** `-0.2597*sqrt(A) + 0.9123*cos(log(A + 1))`

This has two basis functions: `sqrt(A)` and `cos(log(A + 1))`.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

### Candidate 1: `c0 + c1*cos(c2*log(c3*|A| + 1)) + c4*sin(c5*log(c6*|A| + 1) + c7)`

With A ≥ 0, |A| = A. Set c0=0, c2=1, c3=1 for the cos term. The sin term: `c4*sin(c5*log(c6*A + 1) + c7)`. Can sin match sqrt(A)? No - sin of log is oscillatory, sqrt is monotonic. But wait, we can set c4=0 to kill the sin term, leaving `c1*cos(log(A+1))`. That gives only the cos part, missing sqrt(A). We need both terms. Can we use the sin term to produce sqrt(A)? No, sin(log(...)) cannot equal sqrt(A).

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 2: Rational functions times cos(log(...))

This is a sum of rational functions in A and rational×cos(log(...)). Combining over common denominator `(Ac1+c2)`: `[A*c0 + c6 + c8 + (Ac3+c7)*cos(c4*log(c5|A|+1))]/(Ac1+c2)`. This gives `(linear in A + linear×cos(log))/(linear in A)`. This cannot produce sqrt(A).

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 3: `c0 + c1*cos(c2*log(c3*|A| + 1)) + c4*cos(c5*log(c6*|A| + c7))`

Two cos(log(...)) terms plus constant. Cannot produce sqrt(A).

Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 4: `A*c0/(A*c1 + c2) + c3 + c4*exp(c5*sin(c6*log(c7*|A| + 1) + c8))`

Rational function + exp(sin(log(...))). Cannot produce sqrt(A) or cos(log(A+1)).

Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 5: `A*c0 + c1*exp(A*c2) + c3 + c4*exp(c5*cos(c6*log(c7*|A| + 1)))`

Linear, exponential, exp(cos(log(...))). Cannot produce sqrt(A) or cos(log(A+1)).

Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 6: Rational functions + rational×log terms

All rational functions of A and log terms. Cannot produce sqrt(A) or cos(log(A+1)).

Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 7: `c0 + c1*|A|^c2 + c3*exp(c4*sin(c5*log(c6*|A| + 1) + c7))`

With A≥0: `c0 + c1*A^c2 + c3*exp(c4*sin(c5*log(c6*A+1)+c7))`. Set c2=0.5 to get sqrt(A). The exp(sin(log(...))) term: can this equal cos(log(A+1))? No - exp of sin is always positive and has different functional form than cos. These are fundamentally different basis functions.

Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 8: `A^c0 * c1 + c2 + c3*cos(c4*log(c5*|A| + 1))`

Set c0=0.5: `c1*sqrt(A) + c2 + c3*cos(c4*log(c5*A+1))`. Set c4=1, c5=1: `c1*sqrt(A) + c2 + c3*cos(log(A+1))`. Set c1=-0.2597, c2=0, c3=0.9123. This matches GT!

### Candidate 9: `sqrt(A)*c0 + c1 + c2*cos(c3*log(c4*|A| + 1))`

Set c0=-0.2597, c1=0, c3=1, c4=1, c2=0.9123. This matches GT exactly!

Candidate 9 verdict: [MATCH]
